<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10501987067593885096">Pestered by her close New Jersey family, Stephanie Plum offers to catch high-school crush Joe Morelli, cop turned bail jumper, for her cousin Vinnie's company. She questions "working girls" to find the missing girlfriend of vicious prizefighter Benito Ramirez while Joe secretly watches her back. Ranger mentors her and supplies vehicles when hers explode.</span>

      </div>

        $('edition_9264097').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_9264097').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_9264097').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script></div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_313732070">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313732070" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/405390-kemper" class="left imgcol" title="Kemper"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451574879p2/405390.jpg" alt="Kemper" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/313732070?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 19, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/405390-kemper" class="user" title="Kemper">Kemper</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=craptacular" class="actionLinkLite">craptacular</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2012" class="actionLinkLite">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer313732070">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12943648568939832557">It’s Gender Reversal Day here on Goodreads as I review <em>One for the Money</em>. <br /><br />So Samuel Plum is an underwear buyer for a retail store who has recently lost his job. Desperate for cash, he blackmails his pervert cousin who runs a bail bonds agency into letting him go after a cop named Jane Morellie who was accused of murder and then skipped. There may be a personal revenge motive for Samuel in this because Jane is the girl who seduced him and took his virginity in high school. Since she never called</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12943648568939832557">It’s Gender Reversal Day here on Goodreads as I review <em>One for the Money</em>. <br /><br />So Samuel Plum is an underwear buyer for a retail store who has recently lost his job. Desperate for cash, he blackmails his pervert cousin who runs a bail bonds agency into letting him go after a cop named Jane Morellie who was accused of murder and then skipped. There may be a personal revenge motive for Samuel in this because Jane is the girl who seduced him and took his virginity in high school. Since she never called him again, Samuel felt justified in running her over with a car and breaking her leg shortly after that. <br /><br />Now Jane is worth $10,000. Even though he has absolutely no experience or training in law enforcement or as a bounty hunter, Samuel decides he’s going to capture her. He almost immediately stumbles across Jane who basically laughs at him and walks away. So Samuel gets a pistol he doesn’t know how to use or even load. He also allows his senile grandfather to get a hold of the gun because who doesn’t love it when the elderly start waving handguns around in a room full of family members?<br /><br />Samuel’s inexperience quickly gets him into more trouble after he gets assaulted by a female boxer who tries to rape him. Rather than pull his gun on the boxer, he panics and hits her with his man purse. Things get even worse as Jane repeatedly shows up to humiliate him and then get away again. Samuel also gets another person shot when a fugitive takes away his man purse with the gun while Samuel just stands there and allows it to happen. Plus, Samuel’s failure to report the boxer to the police for the attack on him because he doesn’t want to look weak allows two innocent people to be brutally raped and assaulted.<br /><br />Samuel is obviously a moron who has no business running around with a gun and hand cuffs. He also seems to be criminally negligent, and he probably should have been in prison already for running over a sex partner. He also steals Jane’s car when he gets tired of driving his own piece of shit so even though he’s supposedly on the side of law and order, he’s guilty of carrying a concealed weapon and grand theft auto. <br /><br />Samuel is such a nitwit that I have no idea how I’m supposed to relate or sympathize with him. If this was some kind of comic farce, then I could see how a loser getting humiliated by the fugitives he’s supposed to be chasing would be funny, but that kind of goes out the window with the psychotic rapist boxer thing and people getting shot due to Samuel’s utter failure as a bounty hunter.<br /><br />In conclusion, I’ll say that Samuel Plum is a fucktarded asshat who should be beaten with….Oh, wait. Gender Reversal Day was yesterday? And it’s <em>Stephanie</em> Plum, not Samuel? Oh….. I guess in that case she’s just a spunky heroine and her vehicular assault on a former lover, overall gross incompetence and insistence on trying to do a job she has no training or qualifications for is just another example of womanly independence. Girl Power!<br /><br />Now, Stephanie, if you’d just step into this dark alley, there’s a few ladies who’d like a word with you. Oh, don’t worry, it’s just FBI Special Agent Clarice Starling, US Marshal Karen Sisco, Ree Dolly from the Ozarks and Lisbeth Salander from Sweden. They’d like to have a little talk regarding what you’ve done to the image of female heroes in crime fiction. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12943648568939832557">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_20136950">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20136950" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/633779-claire-greene" class="left imgcol" title="Claire Greene"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1206563108p2/633779.jpg" alt="Claire Greene" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20136950?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 14, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/633779-claire-greene" class="user" title="Claire Greene">Claire Greene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20136950">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3908338716099862370">I. LOVE. THESE. BOOKS. SERIOUSLY. I am obsessed with this series. And you know when your brain keeps telling you that this is ridiculous, there must be a hundred books that are written better, or a better mystery, or whatever? Well, I don't care!!! This series is my ultimate guilty pleasure. I was hooked with the first one and have read the entire series thus far - including all the stupid mini books in-between. Now, those mini books I could do without and they always feel like an attempt to mak</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3908338716099862370">I. LOVE. THESE. BOOKS. SERIOUSLY. I am obsessed with this series. And you know when your brain keeps telling you that this is ridiculous, there must be a hundred books that are written better, or a better mystery, or whatever? Well, I don't care!!! This series is my ultimate guilty pleasure. I was hooked with the first one and have read the entire series thus far - including all the stupid mini books in-between. Now, those mini books I could do without and they always feel like an attempt to make sure they even got the loose change in my pockets, but I still get them anyway because it is like a fix until I can get the real thing. So what is so great about them? Stephanie - hilarious. I laugh out loud (a rarity for me when reading a book) constantly when reading these books. I love the murder mysteries which are often at least a step above the formula ones. I love the triangle between Ranger and Morelli and Stephanie. That is something that often gets old for me in other books or TV shows, etc. but for some reason, it just doesn't get old here for me. 13 books in and I am still captivated by the tension between the three. I love the setting - being from CT and living in NY and knowing people from Jersey - she nails that dead on! I mean, an exaggeration of it but still.... And the quirky characters. I love that. I like books that the people are really odd and funny. But it still has to be believable - I hate odd just for the sake of odd - like, hey look at me - I'm wacky - wocka wocka!! But these characters are so outrageous and I still find myself being able to believe it and go along with the book. Do things get repetitive? Sure, I mean, she blows up a car in every single book. But for me, that makes it all the more funny - I can't help it, I laugh every single time. I love how she is so clumsy and crazy and manages to get things done in spite of herself. I love how she is always battling her weight - that constant struggle between carrots and carrot cake! I love her family, the situations she gets in, her friends, her grandmother.... Really, did I mention I love these books? I can't explain it, but I am compulsive about buying the next one as soon as it comes out in paperback and I have kept the entire set and read it through again a few times. I feel that the story just gets better and better as you know the characters more and she doesn't have to spend time introducing them, she can just get on to the chaos. I tried to talk my mom into reading these books and she just couldn't get past the introduction to Morelli (which IS pretty odd - basically two kids experimenting - I just ignore it and skipped beyond it and was able to enjoy the rest of it) and all - I think she was a little too uptight (sorry mom!) to enjoy the whole feel of the series. If I had to sum up the series, I think it would have to be Funny, fast and loose!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3908338716099862370">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1187530833">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14910777567496607712">Just as I predicted, I did not enjoy this.<br /><br />The main character is a LITERAL marshmallow and I absolutely couldn't stand her, and the plot was boring to say the least (it was also ridiculous). I've heard from many people that this book is funny, but I sure didn't think so... It wasn't even like there were jokes that I just didn't see the humor in, but rather I couldn't even understand what was SUPPOSED to be funny about it. The writing was very bland. <br /><br />I also listened to this on audiobook, which is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14910777567496607712">Just as I predicted, I did not enjoy this.<br /><br />The main character is a LITERAL marshmallow and I absolutely couldn't stand her, and the plot was boring to say the least (it was also ridiculous). I've heard from many people that this book is funny, but I sure didn't think so... It wasn't even like there were jokes that I just didn't see the humor in, but rather I couldn't even understand what was SUPPOSED to be funny about it. The writing was very bland. <br /><br />I also listened to this on audiobook, which is the only reason I managed to get through it. I listened to it while I drove and while I was at the gym, so I had no way to escape from it. The narrator was nice to listen to at first (imagine Kat Dennings with a New Jersey accent), but her voice quickly got on my nerves. The only reason I put myself through this torture was because of a reading challenge I'm participating in, where I had to read a book published the year I was born. 1994 was not a great year for book releases.<br /><br />I'm just glad the book was so short so now it's over, and I never have to get inside Stephanie Plum's empty head again. </span>

      <a href="/user/show/5691412-meg" class="user" title="Meg ?">Meg ?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5691412-meg?shelf=e-books" class="actionLinkLite">e-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5691412-meg?shelf=favs" class="actionLinkLite">favs</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5691412-meg?shelf=z-2011-reads" class="actionLinkLite">z-2011-reads</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer223048436">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7386831162249880907">The movie came out a few weeks ago, and I haven't seen it yet. I figured this would be a good time to write a review about this book, since I read it a few months ago, but never got a chance to review it.<br /><br /><br />This book was highly recommended to me, because although I really do read a bit of everything I find chick-lit to be the most entertaining. When I'm in a bad mood I can sit down with a chick-lit about some crazy chick with usually unrealistic problems that makes my life seem boring and laugh my</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7386831162249880907">The movie came out a few weeks ago, and I haven't seen it yet. I figured this would be a good time to write a review about this book, since I read it a few months ago, but never got a chance to review it.<br /><br /><br />This book was highly recommended to me, because although I really do read a bit of everything I find chick-lit to be the most entertaining. When I'm in a bad mood I can sit down with a chick-lit about some crazy chick with usually unrealistic problems that makes my life seem boring and laugh my butt off until my mood perks up. Chick-lit is like chocolate to me in that way.<br /><br /><br />I know that comedy is subjective, but I didn't laugh reading this book once. I don't get it. That was supposedly this books biggest selling point. Also, I was able to read the whole thing since it was super short, but I thought about quitting this one about 10 times in a very short period. Why? It just wasn't that interesting. Stephanie is a broke girl who decides to become a bounty hunter to make money. The first person she needs to pick up is a guy that she hooked up with years ago. Most of the book seemed really corny to me, and that's saying a lot, considering I normally don't mind that in chick-lits. The plot was pretty boring, predictable and unable to hold my attention.<br /><br /><br />The characters. They were genuine and felt real, but again didn't interest me at all. The love triangle starts from book one, and now here we are several years, and many books later and apparently that's still her big choice? <br /><br /><br />Needless to say this is one of the most hyped, critically acclaimed chick-lits I have ever heard of. Everyone who is into cozies always says this is the best. Also, everyone who recommended it said those things like "I'm hooked" or "You will NOT be able to put this one down!"...Me? Not so much.<br /><br /><br />I'm wondering if I'm missing something here or if the series just improves greatly as the books go on. Right now after reading "One for the Money" I don't think Stephanie, her love triangle, and her strange family are people I want to invest the time in. There are like 18 books so far to this series now I think. I will probably try #2 in the future since everyone highly recommended this series to me, and some have insisted that it get's better.<br /><br /><br />This book obviously has tons of fans so I recommend if you like chick-lit give it a try and see how you like it. I feel like I'm one of the only women in the world who isn't a fan of this series, but oh well.<br /><br />I will stick with Sophie Kinsella for my chick-lit fixes from now on.<br /><br />1.5/5 stars</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7386831162249880907">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer81777599">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10353926672772009037">I've been seeing Evanovich books for years and not even once was I compelled to give them another look or find out if they were worth my time. I kind of regret it now.<br /><br />This 1st book in the series about a female bounty hunter set in New Jersey ethnic neighborhood was quite a pleasure to read. The book was written about 15 years ago and definitely felt dated in many ways, especially in regards to "fashion" - spandex shorts, big hair, hoop earrings and all that. But the humor remained fresh, Plum/Mo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10353926672772009037">I've been seeing Evanovich books for years and not even once was I compelled to give them another look or find out if they were worth my time. I kind of regret it now.<br /><br />This 1st book in the series about a female bounty hunter set in New Jersey ethnic neighborhood was quite a pleasure to read. The book was written about 15 years ago and definitely felt dated in many ways, especially in regards to "fashion" - spandex shorts, big hair, hoop earrings and all that. But the humor remained fresh, Plum/Morelli dynamic duo was a lot of fun to follow, and the mystery involving Hispanic and Italian gangsters, prostitutes, a crazy boxer and drugs was an original one.<br /><br />I am not rushing into reading the 2nd book in the series, mostly because I don't want to overdose on them and there is like a million books in the series, so catching up is impossible. But I will definitely check the next book out whenever I am in a mood for a fast-paced funny mystery.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10353926672772009037">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11850022504556281734">Buddy reading with some friends at <strong> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles">Buddies Books and Baubles</a> </strong> starting Nov 1 <br /><br /><strong>The Plan:</strong> Read one book in the series per month.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText11850022504556281734">Buddy reading with some friends at <strong>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles">Buddies Books and Baubles</a>
</strong> starting Nov 1 <br /><br /><strong>The Plan:</strong> Read one book in the series per month. So that's like the next 2 years. I now plan buddy reads 2 years out....no I do not have a problem...and even if I did I seem to be going to a group for it...soooooo. Don't judge me :P<br /><br />Lazy Review Time - <em>since this came out forever ago and there are a bazillion reviews</em><br /><br />This series has 20+ books in it. I can see what it has been so popular over the years. It is just a good time wrapped up in a ball and transported to the 90s. A time when New Jersey was known for garbage and hydrocarbons and people still had answering machines and no cell phones….YES we used to live like that.<br /><br />Stephanie Plum is a fun character and this was a pretty good introductory book with funny shenanigans as she tries to figure out how to be a bounty hunter. She makes some pretty big mistakes that lead to a little bit of hilarity along the way. She is easy to like and I had a good time hanging out with her as she learns the ropes Eliza Doolittle style from a guy named Ranger that I could help but picture in my head as Dog the Bounty Hunter. <br /><br />A few things I liked:<br /><br />? - The Nostalgia I felt for the 90s<br /><br />? - The hinted at future romantic interest *crosses finger* I really liked Morelli and hope they ‘Play Train’ sooner rather than later.<br /><br />? - Crazy Shenanigans i.e. hitting the boy who took your virginity and didn’t call with your car a few years later. (don’t worry he was okay)<br /><br />? - Crazy Grandma’s. I love funny and ridiculous family members so this fit the bill well<br /><br />? - Totally creepy psychopaths. The messed up in the head bad guy is a bit deranged and pretty scary.<br /><br />Definitely and easy fun and funny read with a little drama and suspense. <br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_28837259">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28837259" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/931455-dorothy" class="left imgcol" title="Dorothy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1407125020p2/931455.jpg" alt="Dorothy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/28837259?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 27, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/931455-dorothy" class="user" title="Dorothy">Dorothy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mystery lovers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/931455-dorothy?shelf=modern-day-mysteries" class="actionLinkLite">modern-day-mysteries</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/931455-dorothy?shelf=tough-women" class="actionLinkLite">tough-women</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/931455-dorothy?shelf=re-reading" class="actionLinkLite">re-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer28837259">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer781725898289181270">How is it that, having been an avid reader of mysteries for much of my life, I had never picked up one of Janet Evanovich's Stephanie Plum books? A gross oversight on my part that I have now rectified. I have finished the first one of the series.<br /><br />I've been reading quite a few serious books this summer - "The Maytrees," "Falling Man," "Absolute Friends," and "A Thousand Splendid Suns" to name the most recent - and I was ready for a drastic change. This book certainly offered that.<br /><br />I was captivated</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText781725898289181270">How is it that, having been an avid reader of mysteries for much of my life, I had never picked up one of Janet Evanovich's Stephanie Plum books? A gross oversight on my part that I have now rectified. I have finished the first one of the series.<br /><br />I've been reading quite a few serious books this summer - "The Maytrees," "Falling Man," "Absolute Friends," and "A Thousand Splendid Suns" to name the most recent - and I was ready for a drastic change. This book certainly offered that.<br /><br />I was captivated by the personality of Stephanie from the very first chapter and I found it hard to put the book down. I just couldn't wait to see what happened to her next. As a result, I read the book within 24 hours and most of it in one sitting.<br /><br />This, of course, was the book that introduced Stephanie, her family and friends to the reading public. We get to know her as a very smart woman who has had some hard knocks but is still standing. She has a loving, if annoying and sometimes embarrassing, family.<br /><br />And she has loyal friends from the "burg" where she grew up. One of those "friends," Joe Morelli, plays a very large role in this adventure and apparently in the Plum adventures to come in the series.<br /><br />This book has everything one can ask of a mystery. The plot and the pacing are brisk. The protagonist is attractive and both tough and vulnerable. The repartee is engaging. All in all, a thoroughly satisfying read. On to "Two for the Dough." <br /><br /><u>UPDATE 01/26/12:</u> This was the selection of my local Mystery Book Club this month and so I reread it - or at least most of it - to remind myself of its plot. I found it just as enjoyable the second time around. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="781725898289181270">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/6289182-tilly-slaton" class="user" title="Tilly Slaton">Tilly Slaton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6289182-tilly-slaton?shelf=reviews-completed" class="actionLinkLite">reviews-completed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer228033920">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17531061987726132254">One for the Money is a wonderful book! (REPOSTING DUE TO MOVIE RELEASE!)<br /><br />I have always read psycho-thrillers, romance, paranormal romance etc. My momma told me, “You have to read Evanovich! You’ll laugh so hard!”<br /><br />So, I did.<br /><br />Stephanie Plum is a super cool character. She’s like any regular woman in the world, a fun personality shaped with a loving family, embarrassing moments and some bitter days. She lost her job. Her car was repossessed. She was forced to resort to accepting a job with her cousin V</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17531061987726132254">One for the Money is a wonderful book! (REPOSTING DUE TO MOVIE RELEASE!)<br /><br />I have always read psycho-thrillers, romance, paranormal romance etc. My momma told me, “You have to read Evanovich! You’ll laugh so hard!”<br /><br />So, I did.<br /><br />Stephanie Plum is a super cool character. She’s like any regular woman in the world, a fun personality shaped with a loving family, embarrassing moments and some bitter days. She lost her job. Her car was repossessed. She was forced to resort to accepting a job with her cousin Vinnie.<br /><br />A bounty hunter! She isn’t quite sure where to start. Her nerves are a little jittery and she doesn’t really have a clue what she’s doing. Talk about a blast!<br /><br />Joe Morelli is a charming, sexy man from her past. Playing tunnels and trains when they were 6 and then taking her virginity at age 16 behind the pastry counter. Years afterwards, Stephanie saw him walking down a sidewalk and hopped the curb with her car and bounced him off the hood. Bonus! Pay backs rock!<br /><br />Stephanie’s first day on the job, her first FTA, failure to appear, is Joe Morelli himself! Hilarious. The relationship is fiery. He’s a cop trying to prove his innocence of the murder charges against him. She’s a bounty hunter, a woman from his past, and she is relentless.<br /><br />Grandma Mazur is one of neatest characters I’ve ever read. Imagine your grandma, holding your gun at the dinner table. She’s all excited about you becoming a bounty hunter. She gets your gun to show it off to your family and the man they are trying to set you up with. Somehow, she loads the gun and BAM! She shoots the cooked chicken sitting in the middle of the table!<br /><br />Several dangerous bumps in the road. Although I love heart pounding dramatic moments, there are a few scenes in this book that were worthy of “covering my eyes during a really scary part during a movie.” The details become very gruesome and I wasn’t sure if I was going to bother reading the second book.<br /><br />In the end, the unpredictable ending, the revenge that is taken, the justice that rips through the bad guys was awe-inspiring.<br /><br />I have read this series before. I do recommend this book and series to anyone that needs a laugh. The second book, Two for the Dough is off the charts better than the first. If One for the Money doesn’t make you run for Two for the Dough, just take a deep breath and read the second one.<br /><br />The relationships that are formed are so funny. I was sitting on the couch and I couldn’t stop laughing. My chest burned for air while my family stared at me wondering what was happening. Two for the Dough is beyond hilarious. If you are trying to read and others are sleeping, move as far away from them as possible. Your laughter will shatter their sleep <br /><br />This book should not be read by children or immature young adults.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17531061987726132254">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_124204304">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124204304" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2016128-the-holy-terror" class="left imgcol" title="The Holy Terror"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1447986880p2/2016128.jpg" alt="The Holy Terror" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/124204304?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 16, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2016128-the-holy-terror" class="user" title="The Holy Terror">The Holy Terror</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1659377.One_For_The_Money" title="Audio Cassette 9780788704499" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2016128-the-holy-terror?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2016128-the-holy-terror?shelf=audiobooks" class="actionLinkLite">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2016128-the-holy-terror?shelf=forgot-to-drink-the-kool-aid" class="actionLinkLite">forgot-to-drink-the-kool-aid</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2016128-the-holy-terror?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer124204304">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8166035313758791619">Book:    <br />Narration:   <br />I'm new to audiobooks, and at this point I'm not exactly sure how much they're for me. I can listen to whatever I want during my workday, so I figure, why not catch up on some reading while I do it? The problem is, I seem to come across more audiobooks that rub me the wrong way than those that don't. <strong>When the narrator is female and she reads the part of a male and is trying to either be sexy or menacing, I have a hard time with it.</strong> The same goes the other way as well. I've</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8166035313758791619">Book: ? ? ½ <br />Narration: ? ½ <br />I'm new to audiobooks, and at this point I'm not exactly sure how much they're for me. I can listen to whatever I want during my workday, so I figure, why not catch up on some reading while I do it? The problem is, I seem to come across more audiobooks that rub me the wrong way than those that don't. <strong>When the narrator is female and she reads the part of a male and is trying to either be sexy or menacing, I have a hard time with it.</strong> The same goes the other way as well. I've tried getting through <a title="Odd Thomas (Odd Thomas Novel, #1) by Dean Koontz" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1160083.Odd_Thomas__Odd_Thomas_Novel___1_">Odd Thomas</a> but when the narrator speaks for Odd's girlfriend, I can't help but imagine a drag queen. <strong>It's that jarring that it takes me out of the story, and the same thing happened in this book as well.</strong><br /><br /><strong>I enjoyed this story for what it was: a down on her luck Jersey girl who decides to try her hand at bounty hunting and hilarity ensues.</strong> I didn't find myself laughing all that much, although I did smile at some of Morelli's lines, but then quickly cringed at the sound of the female voicing them. It was a weird experience.<br /><br /><strong>Throughout the novel, Stephanie isn't all that smart.</strong> This being the first in a very long series, I expected that going in, so I wasn't all that surprised when she decided to hit her would-be rapist over the head with her purse instead of taking her gun out of said purse and pointing it at his face. <strong>She doesn't do so many dumb things that it made me want to slap her though, and that can be a fine line to cross.</strong> I actually thought a lot of characters toed that line; her Mom was pushy but in a funny way, her Grandma was crazy but not annoying, and Morelli played sexy and dangerous in a delicious way. Ranger, I'm on the fence about because he played such a small part, and also because I think some of his lines would have been sexier in my head than out of a woman's mouth.<br /><br /><strong>I was surprised at some of the darker parts of this book, although now that I think of it, this kind of reads like a Lifetime movie.</strong> Think murder, torture, rape, all that fun stuff. Throw in some prostitution and drugs and now we're having a good time! Honestly though, I think the grittier bits made me like the story more because it wasn't just fluffy chick-lit all the time, but then, I'm twisted like that.<br /><br /><strong>I liked that I was kept guessing up until the end.</strong> I had my suspicions, but I was actually wrong and I enjoyed that! All too often I figure out the mystery before half the novel is over but that wasn't the case here so that was a pleasant surprise.<br /><br /><strong>I don't think the narrator did a poor job for most of the novel; it was just the sexy and evil men that she was trying to do that wasn't working for me.</strong> I feel like I was missing out on some of the atmosphere with the characters by not hearing the men in my head. Maybe this isn't an issue for others that are used to one narrator doing a whole cast of characters, but it just isn't something that's clicking with me.<br /><br /><strong>I will continue on with this story, but in regular ol' book form.</strong> I hear the love triangle continues on for eternity, but I think I've proved I'm a glutton for punishment since I'm still reading Anita Blake, so I'll definitely pick up the next installment of Stephanie Plum's series soon.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8166035313758791619">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer579759279">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5313286654883057372">My mom's been bugging me for years to read this. I resisted, because, well, mom books. I thought it would be silly, I thought it would be overwrought, I thought it would be chick-lit...and it wasn't! I was pleasantly surprised. It's no deep, mystery-thriller, but it wasn't a complete throw-away beach read, either. I enjoyed it and I'll get #2 on hold from the library. This looks like a good fill in read, a go-to read when I have nothing on tap and need a capable stand in. <br /><br />Thanks Mom!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_282772610">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282772610" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/76688-eric" class="left imgcol" title="Eric"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1255373698p2/76688.jpg" alt="Eric" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/282772610?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 26, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/76688-eric" class="user" title="Eric">Eric</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13384054-one-for-the-money" title="Paperback 9780241957035" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I couldn't in good conscience recommend anyone else read this</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/76688-eric?shelf=audiobooks" class="actionLinkLite">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/76688-eric?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer282772610">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12505495046829843069">My wife and I were heading to Philadelphia for a long weekend, and decided to get an audiobook for the road trip. After a short conversation about how that "female bounty hunter movie" was based on a best selling book, I downloaded this. I was slightly curious, as I have seen the author's name on bookshelves for years now, and didn't know anything other than that she was very fond of numbers in her titles. <br /><br />Eight minutes into our road trip my wife asked me to shut the book off, as she had a heada</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12505495046829843069">My wife and I were heading to Philadelphia for a long weekend, and decided to get an audiobook for the road trip. After a short conversation about how that "female bounty hunter movie" was based on a best selling book, I downloaded this. I was slightly curious, as I have seen the author's name on bookshelves for years now, and didn't know anything other than that she was very fond of numbers in her titles. <br /><br />Eight minutes into our road trip my wife asked me to shut the book off, as she had a headache. All we heard was a childhood flashback about the main character getting tricked by a neighborhood kid into playing "train tunnel" in her pants. I was happy to acquiesce, as I thought both the book and the narrator were dreadful. <br /><br />But now I feel compelled to finish what I started, since I paid for it, and I have to listen to something while commuting in rush hour traffic. So either the book is going to improve significantly, or I am going to have fun writing a scathing review when it's finally over.<br /><br />UPDATE:<br /><br />I finished listening to this yesterday. It was beyond awful. <br /><br />The main character, Stephanie Plum, makes stupid decision after stupid decision. In fact, I cannot think of a single rational, logical decision she made at any point in the novel. And all the while, the reader is subjected to constant descriptions of her clothing, jewelry and make-up. <br /><br />Supporting characters around her appear and disappear, serving only as thinly veiled plot devices. Her family, her boss and Ranger are never mentioned after the half-way point of the novel. I lost count of how many times Plum catches up to Morelli only to not even try to apprehend him. <br /><br />Deus ex machina moments occur regularly. More than one character seems clinically schizophrenic. The "mystery" would have never been solved, if not for a <a rel="nofollow" href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/EvilGloating?from=Main.Monologuing">lengthy expository speech</a> by the villain right before he plans to kill the protagonist. <br /><br />No way would I ever pick up another one of these books. Oh, and why am I not surprised to learn that Janet Evanovich is one of Stephenie Meyer's favorite authors? </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12505495046829843069">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_143598292">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143598292" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4859890-jubilation-lee" class="left imgcol" title="Jubilation Lee"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1296010539p2/4859890.jpg" alt="Jubilation Lee" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/143598292?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 05, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4859890-jubilation-lee" class="user" title="Jubilation Lee">Jubilation Lee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=where-was-my-parental-supervision" class="actionLinkLite">where-was-my-parental-supervision</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=hello-smex-my-old-friend" class="actionLinkLite">hello-smex-my-old-friend</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=whodunit" class="actionLinkLite">whodunit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=funny-strange-or-funny-ha-ha" class="actionLinkLite">funny-strange-or-funny-ha-ha</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=badass-book-club" class="actionLinkLite">badass-book-club</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=you-go-girl" class="actionLinkLite">you-go-girl</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=but-wait-theres-more" class="actionLinkLite">but-wait-theres-more</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=books-for-baby-birds" class="actionLinkLite">books-for-baby-birds</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=read-in-2012" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4859890-jubilation-lee?shelf=anecdotalicious" class="actionLinkLite">anecdotalicious</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer143598292">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5015764705602217098">When I was in seventh grade, freshly transferred to a new school, my sole friend invited me up to <em>her</em> friend’s mother’s friend’s cabin, to stay for a week with a bunch of kids I’d never met before. I don’t particularly like cabins. I burn in the sun. I don’t swim well. And I’m not good around strangers. So I told her no, and then my mother made me go back to her and say yes.<br /><br />Sigh.<br /><br />So there I was, at a cabin full of strange girls, knowing that at any second we were going to go windsurfing or someth</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5015764705602217098">When I was in seventh grade, freshly transferred to a new school, my sole friend invited me up to <em>her</em> friend’s mother’s friend’s cabin, to stay for a week with a bunch of kids I’d never met before. I don’t particularly like cabins. I burn in the sun. I don’t swim well. And I’m not good around strangers. So I told her no, and then my mother made me go back to her and say yes.<br /><br />Sigh.<br /><br />So there I was, at a cabin full of strange girls, knowing that at any second we were going to go windsurfing or something, and I would be exposed as the only overweight clumsy socially inept tween of the group and I would die right there on the spot and then my mother would be sorry.<br /><br />Seconds before this happened, though, one of the girls pulled the rest of us away from our parental supervision and held up a copy of <em>One for the Money</em>. She had swiped it (along with the next two books in the series) from her mom. And for reasons that sort of bewilder me even to this day, we all sat down en masse in one of the cabin bedrooms and started to read it out loud. <br /><br />This book, guys. It was the most shocking thing I had ever read in my <em>life</em>. We’d be hunched breathless over the pages, whispering key scenes to one another in a giddy pre-teen frenzy. <br /><br /><em>“I know about Madam Zaretski and her whips and chains. I know about the boys. And I know about the duck.” Lucille would throw up if she knew what he did to the duck. Then she'd tell her father, Harry the Hammer, and Harry would cut off Vinnie's dick.</em> <br /><br />And then we’d burst into hysterical laughter, repeating lines to one another (His <em>dick!</em> He’d have it cut off! Have you ever <em>heard</em> anything so awesome?!) while the parents in the house yelled at us to cut down the noise and go <em>outside</em>, for God’s sake, we were at a <em>cabin</em> and should be taking advantage of the good weather. <br /><br />I’m not sure where this story was going, except to say that <em>One for the Money</em> is directly responsible for friendships I still have to this day, and may singlehandedly have saved my teen years, and I don’t care how ridiculous and fluffy and pointless it is, because I will love it forever.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5015764705602217098">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/87302-marin" class="user" title="Marin">Marin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer31633395">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6621082283580443440">I wanted to like this book. I have been watching the growth of the chick lit genre with interest, especially in the sub-sub-genre of chick-lit legal thrillers and mysteries. I think there's cool stuff happening here.<br /><br />Unfortunatley, I'm not a fan of this book, and I won't be continuing this series. I was looking for something easy and breezy, but not dumb. Stephanie Plum, the main character, made decisions that didn't make sense to me. I suppose the writer could have described the complex emotions</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6621082283580443440">I wanted to like this book. I have been watching the growth of the chick lit genre with interest, especially in the sub-sub-genre of chick-lit legal thrillers and mysteries. I think there's cool stuff happening here.<br /><br />Unfortunatley, I'm not a fan of this book, and I won't be continuing this series. I was looking for something easy and breezy, but not dumb. Stephanie Plum, the main character, made decisions that didn't make sense to me. I suppose the writer could have described the complex emotions that might lead a female bounty hunter to kiss a man she knows is wanted for murder rather than pepper spray him, handcuff him, and haul him into jail. The author's explanation, from Stephanie Plum's point of view: "He sure knew how to kiss." What? <br /><br />Also I felt like the bubblegum quality of the writing was jarring when it was discussing serious subjects such as torture and rape. Linda Fairstein, Patricia Cornwall, and Lisa Scottoline all do a better job.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6621082283580443440">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/21266950?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 06, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/925549-miss-kim" class="user" title="Miss Kim">Miss Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/925549-miss-kim?shelf=2008" class="actionLinkLite">2008</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/925549-miss-kim?shelf=she-is-tstl" class="actionLinkLite">she-is-tstl</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/925549-miss-kim?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer21266950">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5391887766946247093">So I've finally met Stephanie Plum. I wasn't disappointed. I read this in a matter of hours, and laughed most of the time. She gets fired from her job, so she goes to work for her cousin Vinnie as a bounty hunter. Needing big cash, she takes the case of Joe Morelli, a cop wanted for murder. She stumbles her way through everything from stealing cars, shooting guns, catching Failure to Appears. I like her because she suffers the indignities of the everyday woman--bad hair, etc. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/2098381-heather" class="left imgcol" title="Heather"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1374231830p2/2098381.jpg" alt="Heather" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/85539846?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 18, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2098381-heather" class="user" title="Heather">Heather</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer85539846">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1776726273106045809">Stephanie Plum has hit some hard times. She’s lost her job as a buyer of cheap lingerie, fallen behind on her bills and has had her beloved car repossessed. She’s got moldy cheese and a stale loaf of bread in the fridge and she has hawked most of her furniture and major appliances to pay the rent and procure a P.O.S Nova. Stephanie doubts things could get much worse. She’s about to be proven wrong.<br /><br />In a stroke of dumb luck, or perhaps, an evil twist of fate, Stephanie lands a job at her uncle Vin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1776726273106045809">Stephanie Plum has hit some hard times. She’s lost her job as a buyer of cheap lingerie, fallen behind on her bills and has had her beloved car repossessed. She’s got moldy cheese and a stale loaf of bread in the fridge and she has hawked most of her furniture and major appliances to pay the rent and procure a P.O.S Nova. Stephanie doubts things could get much worse. She’s about to be proven wrong.<br /><br />In a stroke of dumb luck, or perhaps, an evil twist of fate, Stephanie lands a job at her uncle Vinnie’s bonding company as a bounty hunter. It’s Stephanie’s duty to bring in FTA’s in exchange for 10% of the bond. When Stephanie is informed about an FTA worth 10 grand, Stephanie is all over it, until she discovers the FTA is none other than Joe Morelli, Stephanie’s childhood nemesis, who taught her how to play train at the age of six and deflowered her behind an éclair case 10 years later. She may have clipped him in the leg with her dad’s Buick three years later, but thoughts of Morelli still rankle. What follows is an amusing, entertaining and at times, pretty sexy man hunt.<br /><br />Stephanie isn’t brilliant, but she certainly isn’t dumb, more hilarious because of her dumb luck than snide humor, she’s a pretty endearing heroine. I enjoyed the time spent with <a title="One for the Money (A Stephanie Plum Novel, #1) by Janet Evanovich" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money__A_Stephanie_Plum_Novel___1_">One for the Money</a> and find myself wanting to dive in to book two as soon as possible. Great way to spend a Sunday.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1776726273106045809">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8827624450782796604">Stephanie Plum: a 6 anni gioca al trenino con Joe Morelli. A 16 gli vende il <em>bignè</em>, nonostante tutti, mamma compresa, continuassero ad avvertirla di stare lontana dal bad boy. Per tanti anni non si sono più cagati, come da copione: Joe Morelli è il tipo da "una botta e via". Ma poi, sulla soglia dei 30, senza uno straccio di lavoro e senza qualcuno da cui farsi mantenere, decide di diventare un'agente di recupero.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText8827624450782796604">Stephanie Plum: a 6 anni gioca al trenino con Joe Morelli. A 16 gli vende il <em>bignè</em>, nonostante tutti, mamma compresa, continuassero ad avvertirla di stare lontana dal bad boy. Per tanti anni non si sono più cagati, come da copione: Joe Morelli è il tipo da "una botta e via". Ma poi, sulla soglia dei 30, senza uno straccio di lavoro e senza qualcuno da cui farsi mantenere, decide di diventare un'agente di recupero. Allettata probabilmente da quei bei soldoni se mai fosse stata in grado di consegnare alla polizia nientepopodimeno che... Morelli.<br /><br />Sentite, a me aveva già convinto a pagina 2.<br />Se poi considerate le innumerevoli gag comiche tra i due (da Morelli che si introduce in casa della Plum e l'ammanetta alla doccia, alla completa immersione nei cassoni dell'immondizia per recuperare le chiavi dell'auto, al diffamare Morelli con delle prostitute), la sbadataggine universalmente riconosciuta di lei, e le assurde situazioni in cui viene coinvolta avete fatto tredici.<br /><br />Oh, è pure breve!<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer538991098">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8321239587534524301">Okay, it's official. This book did not work for me. <br /><br />Let's start with a confession: I am a Jersey girl. That's right, born and bred. Jersey girl from birth to present with a brief Boston interlude for college. <br /><br />So, because of that, I really thought I would click with this series. I love anything funny, I can relate to all things Jersey, and most of my GR friends are crazy about this book. A sure thing, right?? Alas, this book just didn't do it for me. I found it to be really dated, not particularl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8321239587534524301">Okay, it's official. This book did not work for me. <br /><br />Let's start with a confession: I am a Jersey girl. That's right, born and bred. Jersey girl from birth to present with a brief Boston interlude for college. <br /><br />So, because of that, I really thought I would click with this series. I love anything funny, I can relate to all things Jersey, and most of my GR friends are crazy about this book. A sure thing, right?? Alas, this book just didn't do it for me. I found it to be really dated, not particularly funny (I didn't laugh once), and sort of boring. I had to force myself to read 66 pages before I called it quits. I think it is a "it's not you, it's me" sort of deal. Sorry Stephanie Plum, I'm dropping you!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer155007210">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10104145875813362691">This, fittingly, was my introduction to Evanovich. The woman has a way with characters! These people seemed so real, so human, so flawed, so vulnerable, and often so damn funny, I hated to close the book. Luckily, there are many more in the series for me to read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer270582159">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8242363505290045639">The easy review here would be to just bash and toss around a bunch of mehs and ughs and dress it up with "stupid and trashy" and maybe a well placed "crappy pile of claptrap." Truth is, I didn't like it. But a lot of people do and I certainly read enough of what other people consider garbage to want to keep my glass house situated in a stone free environment. <br /><br />I'll just say that this one wasn't for me. There were a few laughs and it moved quickly, but I never found anything to really connect with</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8242363505290045639">The easy review here would be to just bash and toss around a bunch of mehs and ughs and dress it up with "stupid and trashy" and maybe a well placed "crappy pile of claptrap." Truth is, I didn't like it. But a lot of people do and I certainly read enough of what other people consider garbage to want to keep my glass house situated in a stone free environment. <br /><br />I'll just say that this one wasn't for me. There were a few laughs and it moved quickly, but I never found anything to really connect with. I really wish I would have because there are a lot of books in this series and it would have been great to secure this kind of job security in my reading. Oh well, I guess it wasn't meant to be. Damn.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer415768040">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8894456611541730307">I know many love this series and Stephanie Plum. Unfortunately, I just couldn't connect and didn't find her ineptness all that funny. My investigators/detectives have to have some level of smarts, either streetwise or instinctive. That's not Stephanie and this isn't my kind of mystery but completely get how this character and story may be appealing to many. <br /><br />I won't be continuing the series. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a href="/review/show/97311174?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 23, 2012</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer97311174">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7085113175007819308"><br /><br />Honesty time.<br /><br /><br /><br />I'm among the 1%.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="the 1%, monty burns" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693442.jpg" /></a><br /><em>Whoa, folks. Not this 1% (although how awesome would <u>that</u> be? Owning attack hounds. Rocking a monocle. Wearing titanium shoes. Using fancy words like 'indubitably' and 'mustachioed'. I'd be the best billionaire evah.)</em><br /><br />I'm talking about the <em>other</em> 1%. You know, the people who read One for the Money and didn't like it. People such as:<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693443.jpg" /></a><br /><em>The Church Lady</em><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693444.jpg" /></a><br /><em>Grumpy Old Man</em><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693445.jpg" /></a><br /><em>These guys</em><br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://i79.photobucket.com/albums/j127/dpbitner/IMG_0958-1.jpg"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693446.jpg" /></a><br /><em>...Me...</em><br /><br />(I guess this means I'm officially old and boring or whatever.) <br /><br />But yeah, I totally do</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7085113175007819308"><br /><br />Honesty time.<br /><br /><br /><br />I'm among the 1%.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="the 1%, monty burns" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693442.jpg" /></a><br /><em>Whoa, folks. Not this 1% (although how awesome would <u>that</u> be? Owning attack hounds. Rocking a monocle. Wearing titanium shoes. Using fancy words like 'indubitably' and 'mustachioed'. I'd be the best billionaire evah.)</em><br /><br />I'm talking about the <em>other</em> 1%. You know, the people who read One for the Money and didn't like it. People such as:<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693443.jpg" /></a><br /><em>The Church Lady</em><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693444.jpg" /></a><br /><em>Grumpy Old Man</em><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693445.jpg" /></a><br /><em>These guys</em><br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://i79.photobucket.com/albums/j127/dpbitner/IMG_0958-1.jpg">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693446.jpg" /></a><br /><em>...Me...</em><br /><br />(I guess this means I'm officially old and boring or whatever.) <br /><br />But yeah, I totally do not like this book unlike 99% of the GoodReads population. As far as I'm concerned One for the Money is a dated, exceptionally lame version of The Jersey Shore in which everyone is sporting spandex, big hair, and sexist attitudes. <br /><br />So basically it's almost exactly the same as every episode of The Jersey Shore. Except with more guns.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="I'M IN JERSEY SHORE BIIITCH" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693447._SX540_.jpg" /></a><br /><em>Not <u>these</u> guns...</em><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Photobucket" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333744i/693448.jpg" /></a><br /><em>Now that's more like it.</em><br /><br />Exactly like the Jersey Shore with lots of real guns. And a really dumb grown woman who cannot be bothered to learn how to shoot a gun even though she's carrying one with her at all times. <br /><br />Why, you ask? <br /><br />Because she's being stalked by a rapist. A really violent, super-dangerous raping-rapist who totally wants to rape her. A lot. <br /><br />But that's not all, folks. There is also a really mysterious mystery. (A rape-y mystery.) <br /><br />This really attractive MENSA candidate wrapped in spandex who can't shoot a gun to save her life is named Stephanie Plum. Stephanie is trying to solve a mystery so she can help clear the name and reputation of <s>the guy who sexually assaulted her when they were children</s> the smoosh-worthy <s>skeevy man-whore</s> love interest. All so she can haul him into jail for jumping bail and collect the $20,000 bounty on his head, or whatever. <br /><br />In the meantime sexual tension is building between the two. They're tripping over all the innuendo. It's sexy and mysterious. And full of (dumb-)damsel-in-distress like situations. <br /><br />How could I not love this book, you ask? I just don't. Although, I think I just proved I'm old and boring. If you're not old or boring, and you really love the Jersey Shore, One for the Money might just be the book for you. <br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15390563">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8655643587295909603">Stephanie Plum has just gotten laid off from her job as a lingerie buyer for a company that turned out to be owned by the mob in New Jersey. Her Miata has just been repossessed, she's sold everything of value, and her refrigerator is empty. Out of desperation, she goes to see her cousin Vinnie, a bail bondsman, about a filing job. That's just been filled, but the secretary lets her know that there's an opening for a bounty hunter, and the money's good. Stephanie blackmails her way into taking a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8655643587295909603">Stephanie Plum has just gotten laid off from her job as a lingerie buyer for a company that turned out to be owned by the mob in New Jersey. Her Miata has just been repossessed, she's sold everything of value, and her refrigerator is empty. Out of desperation, she goes to see her cousin Vinnie, a bail bondsman, about a filing job. That's just been filled, but the secretary lets her know that there's an opening for a bounty hunter, and the money's good. Stephanie blackmails her way into taking a case that will pay out $10,000 if she can bring the guy in. It turns out the fugitive is someone she has a long history with who appears to be a cop gone bad. He's been arrested for cold-blooded murder. Of course, Stephanie is unbelievably unqualified for this job, but a mixture of desperation, pride, and stubborness take her a long way.<br /><br />This was a quick, fun read, but there was still plenty of murder and mayhem for most mystery/thriller readers. <br />This was actually pretty funny. I don't think I ever laughed out loud, but I probably giggled a few times. I had expected it to be a little funnier and less violent from what someone had told me about it, but this was still a good book. One thing that did irritate me was that the author pretty much gave driving directions to every place Stephanie went in the book. That might make it more real to the people from Trenton, NJ, but to me it was just distracting fluff for me to skip over.<br /><br /><br />The characters were what really made the book. You have to like Stephanie. She comes across as just an average woman who's gotten in over her head, but she doesn't let that stop her. The dirtbag characters were really dirtbags. Some of the stuff they did made me want to go take a shower. And Joe was a hottie. What girl doesn't like a good guy with a little bit of bad in him? Or is he a bad boy with a little bit of good in him? Either way, he's sexy. I hope he shows up in other books.<br /><br />So if you like your mysteries with some humor and you don't mind some blood along the way, you'll like this one.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8655643587295909603">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_577789327">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577789327" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j" class="left imgcol" title="Darth J"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442508603p2/18974711.jpg" alt="Darth J" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/577789327?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 25, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j" class="user" title="Darth J">Darth J</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money" title="Paperback 9780312362089" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=plum" class="actionLinkLite">plum</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer577789327">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7299931958735645197">I first read this book in 2004 and I thought it was a really fun quick read. One for the Money is one of those beach reads that you can consume like popcorn, which is no wonder why I picked up a few of the other installments in the Stephanie Plum series as soon as I finished this one. This series manages to stay fresh up until about the tenth or eleventh book, where the same plot is used over and over again and you really become worried that the main character is stuck in a kind of Groundhog Day</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7299931958735645197">I first read this book in 2004 and I thought it was a really fun quick read. One for the Money is one of those beach reads that you can consume like popcorn, which is no wonder why I picked up a few of the other installments in the Stephanie Plum series as soon as I finished this one. This series manages to stay fresh up until about the tenth or eleventh book, where the same plot is used over and over again and you really become worried that the main character is stuck in a kind of Groundhog Day situation. Other than that, you can really enjoy the first book because it isn't as heavy reading as some of the other mysteries out there. Evanovich set up a pretty good franchise with this book, but tanked it with lazy writing later in the series and allowed a really terrible movie adaptation, so don't be swayed by what people are saying about the more recent events in this series. The first one is really worth a gander, just don't watch the movie because it is a poor representation of the source material. <br /><br />If, by some horrible chance you do see the movie, the only good part is Sherri Shepherd as Lula.<br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415817ra/821034.gif" /><br /><br />Review also posted at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://mybookshelfisready.tumblr.com/post/83833633637/one-for-the-money-by-janet-evanovich">My Bookshelf is Ready</a>.</span>

Izzy\'s brother, David, the family\'s most upright member, has adopted an uncharacteristically unkempt appearance and attitude toward work, life, and Izzy. Facing a housing crisis, she can\'t sleep, she can\'t remember where she parked her car, and, despite her shrinks\' persistence, she can\'t seem to break through in her appointments. Nor can she explain exactly how she feels about Detective Henry Stone and his plans to move in with his new Assistant DA girlfriend...Filled with the signature side-splitting Spellman antics, Revenge     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2384.Janet_Evanovich">About Janet Evanovich</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/2384.Janet_Evanovich"><img alt="2384" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1385051483p2/2384.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer354884817465949395">Janet Evanovich is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of the Stephanie Plum series, the Lizzy and Diesel series, twelve romance novels, the Alexandra Barnaby novels and Trouble Maker graphic novel, and How I Write: Secrets of a Bestselling Author, as well as the Fox and O'Hare series with co-author Lee Goldberg.</span>

    </div>

A body turns up in a garbage bag. She’s got a nasty bookie following her around town. Grandma Mazur has her hands on the stun gun. Stephanie can’t keep a car for more than forty-eight hours. Two men are trying to get her into bed. She has nothing to wear to the Mafia wedding. And there’s an angry little man (don’t call him a dwarf!) who won’t leave her apartment.\n\nBail jumping in Trenton is down to small potatoes. Stephanie’s only open case is a small bond for a small violation, committed by a small person who raises Stephanie’s frustration level in big ways. So short of money and long on bills, Stephanie comes up with a plan-–diversify! Signing on as an intern with entrepreneurial Super Bounty Hunter Ranger, Stephanie ventures into Ranger’s mostly morally correct and marginally legal operations.\n\nNone of this makes vice cop Joe Morelli a happy man. The cop in him can’t help but wonder as to the source of Stephanie’s expensive new cars. And the rest of him, the man who’s been friend and lover to Stephanie, can’t help but wonder if there’s more to the partnership than meets the eye.\n\nThe internship is downgraded to second priority when Uncle Fred goes missing. Even though Grandma Mazur is sure he was abducted by aliens, Stephanie sets out to look for Fred. He’s a perfectly average senior citizen, and he’s disappeared without a trace while running errands. He’s left his ten-year-old Pontiac station wagon locked up nice and neat in the Grand Union parking lot, the cleaning is carefully arranged on the back seat, and his wife is at home, waiting for him to return with the bread and the milk and the olive loaf bologna. Locked in the top drawer of his desk are photos of a body, dismembered and stuffed into a garbage bag.
